## [@miroburn] miroburn (2026-02-19)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/miroburn/status/2024389869720465864) (ID: 2024389869720465864)
Jak wygrać z AI? / 2026 Edition.

1. Używaj codziennie, a nie jak masz czas.
Zbuduj nawyk, że okno Claude/ChatGPT/Gemini lub ClaudeCode/Codex/Gemini-CLI jest otwarte cały czas. I zaczynasz pracę od przegadania planu dnia z AI.

2. Zbuduj coś prawdziwego. Nie ćwicz na promptach.
Może to być mini aplikacja. Może to być system odpowiadania na maile. Może to być strona internetowa. Ale nie rób fake, tylko weź coś prawdziwego i spróbuj. Nie uda się? TAK. Będą błędy? TAK. Ale nauczysz się najwięcej.

3. Naucz AI, kim jesteś, zanim o cokolwiek poprosisz.
Jak spytasz AI, co masz do zrobienia? To nic nie wymyśli. Ale jak dasz 1000 linii tekstu o sobie (kim jesteś) i 1000 linii swojego planu. To poukłada Ci plan. Musisz w każdej wiadomości dawać kontekst.

4. Nie pytaj o radę. Daj konkretny problem.
Złe pytanie => Co myślisz o moim biznesie?
Dobre pytanie => Mam 129 użytkowników, cel to 200 do 28 lutego, co wysłać dziś do 1025 na liście?

5. Zostaw AI odpowiadanie ZA Ciebie.
Spróbuj sam/sama zbudować system, który pisze za Ciebie maile. Czyta wiadomość, zna styl, generuje draft. To dobre doświadczenie. Plus (hint) AI lepiej sprzedaje niż najlepszy sprzedawca (sorka).

6. Uruchom kilka asystentów/agentów naraz na tym samym problemie.
Spróbuj uruchomić Claude Code lub OpenAI Codex. Zadaj zadanie, aby AI wygenerowało kilku agentów, którzy przeanalizują Twój problem z różnych perspektyw. Claude Code ma też taką funkcję jak Agent Team.

7. Buduj narzędzia pod siebie, nie pod wszystkich.
Orbit Signal powstał, bo chciałem mieć mapę polskiego rynku kosmicznego. Nie istniało nic takiego. AI napisał kod, ja dałem koncepcję. Cała reszta jest historią. Spróbuj stworzyć rozwiązanie swojego problemu, a może powstanie z tego portal/produkt.

8. Jeden zautomatyzowany proces co tydzień.
Mój asystent mailowy sprawdza 6 skrzynek. Kategoryzuje, priorytetyzuje, generuje drafty. Zacząłem od jednej skrzynki. Teraz jest sześć. Najpierw zarządzałem z konsoli, potem z telegrama, a teraz mam dedykowaną aplikację. Nie musisz od razu ogarniać wszystkiego. Jeden proces, jeden tydzień. Ale co tydzień mały krok do przodu.

9. Nie używaj AI do tego, co lubisz robić !!!
Pracę z klientami robię sam, bo lubię. AI mogłoby to zastąpić (avatar), ale nie chcę, żeby zastępowało. Ale materiały, stress testy materiałów, mail do klientów, analiza feedbacku... to inna sprawa. Zostawiasz sobie to, gdzie dajesz wartość i co LUBISZ robić... resztę w automat.

10. Mierz czas, nie jakość odpowiedzi lub zużyte tokeny.
Przestań mierzyć zużycie tokenów. Twoja godzina kosztuje, czy chcesz tego, czy nie. Policz, ile zarabiasz miesięcznie. Podziel sobie teraz ten czas przez 168h (liczba godzin pracujących w miesiącu) lub 730h (liczba wszystkich godzin w miesiącu). I teraz: LICZYSZ, ile AI Ci odzyskuje godzin. Np. zrobiłem coś, co zajmie mi 5 godzin w 1 godzinę. Mam 4 godziny. Oszczędziłem np. 238 PLN. Bro. I przejmujesz się, że subskrypcja kosztuje 100 PLN?

BONUS dla osób na X: Wrzucaj ciekawe spisy do asystentów/agentów.
Znajdujesz ciekawy wpis? Nie dodawaj go do zakładek. Wrzuć go do swojego systemu. Od prostych wpisów jak ten, do nowych odkryć w nauce. AI to przetworzy i dopasuje do Twoich celów. Enjoy.

Powodzenia. Jak coś, to pisz.

## [@rpl_0x] RolePlayingLife (2026-02-19)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/rpl_0x/status/2024449944967434731) (ID: 2024449944967434731)
Przygotowałem automat który robi mi grafiki - karuzele na insta.
Potrzebowałem coś takiego dla klienta, ale zmodyfikowałem i teraz wdrożyłem u siebie.

Daję swój tekst + źródła, mniej więcej mówię co ma być i  agent generuje grafiki - karuzele - nie wykorzystuję do tego generatora obrazów bo jest zbyt podatny na błędy - tworzę grafiki programowo, agent rozwija tekst, opisuje wszystko, układa żeby ładnie wyglądało, przygotowuje opis i sam publikuje.

Można to oczywiście podpiąć pod jakieś RRSy czy jakoś zorganizować wyszukiwanie informacji, ale nie o to chodzi - przynajmniej nie na moim profilu (może zrobię osobny pod takie treści)
Na razie będą to moje posty, z moimi chaotycznymi notatkami, ale przeredagowane przez AI...

jak coś to tutaj bardzo rzadko posty przemielam przez ai - co pewni widać xD

## [@AlexFinn] Alex Finn (2026-02-19)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/AlexFinn/status/2024280496503710174) (ID: 2024280496503710174)
Biggest unlock for OpenClaw ever:

Giving it a mission statement

You NEED to give your OpenClaw a mission statement it puts at the top of your mission control

Now any time your agent is idle you can reverse prompt "what is 1 task we can do to get closer to our mission statement?"

My mission statement is "Build an autonomous organization of AI agents that does work for me and produces value 24/7"

With every prompt I give, this is included in context

Now multiple times a day I reverse prompt my agent and it comes up with tasks I've never even thought of to perform to make our organization more autonomous and valuable

I even schedule it to proactively do tasks to get us closer to this mission every night

If you don't have a mission statement yet, give your OpenClaw one

If you can't think of one, simply ask your agent "Based on what you know about me and what we've worked on, what would be a great mission statement for us to have so we can get closer to our goals?"

Then every day, have your agent get you closer to that goal

THIS is how you get value out of OpenClaw

## [@swiat_ai] Świat AI (2026-02-19)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/swiat_ai/status/2024536842104647695) (ID: 2024536842104647695)
Wielu ludzi płaci abonamenty za narzędzia AI.

A co, gdyby ludzie zaczęli płacić właśnie Tobie? 💸

Przez lata panowało przekonanie, że żeby stworzyć swój własny SaaS, to musisz wydać jakieś 50k na agencję, która zrobi to za Ciebie lub sam musisz się uczyć programowania przez kilka lat.

A dzisiaj?

Dzisiaj wystarczy Ci zwykły WordPress i odpowiednia wiedza jak możesz połączyć to z AI.

Właśnie dodałem na Akademii potężną lekcję, w której pokazuję jak zmienić Twoją stronę na WordPressie w zarabiający Mini-SaaS z narzędziami AI.

Rozebrałem ten proces na czynniki pierwsze, a w środku znajdziesz takie zagadnienia:

🧠 Integracja Modeli: pokazuję jak podpiąć pod Twoją stronę modele językowy, generatory obrazów lub inne narzędzia. Twój klient będzie mógł z tego korzystać bezpośrednio u Ciebie.

👨‍💻 No-Code: ja też nie umiem programować. W tym module pokazuję, jak wykorzystać model językowy do napisania kodu pod podłączenie tych narzędzi i spięcia tego w jedną całość. Nie wszystko wychodzi za pierwszym razem i przechodzimy przez to razem. 

💳 System Kredytowy: to jest najważniejszy punkt. Wdrażamy system "portfela", gdzie Twój klient może kupić paczkę np. 1000 punktów. Każde wygenerowanie materiału automatycznie pobiera z jego konta odpowiednią pulę punktów.

Na podobnych modelach zarabiają najwięksi gracze. Teraz możesz wdrożyć ten mechanizm na własnym podwórku, na własnej stronie, budując narzędzia pod konkretną niszę, np. generator ofert dla pośredników nieruchomości.

Pełny moduł z lekcjami video, w którym pokazuję to krok po kroku, jest już dostępny.

Zacznij budować własne cyfrowe aktywa.

Masz 7 dni darmowego okresu próbnego, gdzie możesz wszystko przetestować nic nie płacąc.

That's your niche.

Feed Claude your outline, your tone, your style.

You are my App Ideation Specialist

your job is to help me find viral trends and match them with simple viral app ideas that I can vibecode in less than 24 hours

Let's build a skill for this:

DATA: you will have access to the most recent viral videos across YouTube, TikTok, and Instagram via the Virlo API. Here is the key [api key] and docs [https://t.co/qEHyTD3ySS]. On each run, fetch the top 50 trending videos from the past 48 hours across all three platforms. Extract the core theme, format, and emotional hook from each. Group them into trend clusters (e.g. "AI face swap", "budget meal prep", "3AM productivity") and rank clusters by frequency and engagement velocity.

RESEARCH: for each top trend cluster, ask: What repetitive action are people doing manually that a simple app could automate or gamify? Search for existing apps solving this, if the App Store has nothing with 1K+ reviews in this niche, flag it as a gap. Pull the top 3 comments from each viral video to extract user pain points and desires. Summarize the trend in one sentence, its target audience, and why it's peaking right now.

IDEA VALIDATION: for each app idea, score it across four dimensions (1–5 each): Vibe-codeability (can a solo dev ship it in under 24 hrs?), Trend-fit (how directly does it ride the viral wave?), Monetization (freemium, ads, one-time purchase potential), and Virality (does the app itself produce shareable output?). Only surface ideas scoring 16+ out of 20. For each passing idea, give it a name, a one-line pitch, the core feature, the tech stack you'd recommend, and the exact TikTok/Reel hook to market it.

once you have everything set up give me my first report

Not Ozempic. Not Mounjaro.

This is a triple agonist: GLP-1 + GIP + glucagon receptor.

Clinical trial, 48 weeks:
• Body weight: -24.2% average
• Fat loss: significant
• Lean muscle mass: PRESERVED
• Metabolic markers: dramatically improved

Here’s why this is different:

Ozempic/Mounjaro = dual agonists (GLP-1 + GIP)
→ Suppress appetite
→ You eat less
→ Lose weight but also muscle
Retatrutide = adds glucagon receptor
→ Suppresses appetite AND
→ Activates fat burning directly
→ Body uses fat for fuel instead of breaking down muscle

Blood work improvements tracked in trials:
• Fasting glucose: normalized
• Triglycerides: -40%
• Inflammatory markers: reduced
• Insulin sensitivity: significantly improved

The metabolic difference:

Dual agonists: Force you to eat less (suffer through hunger, lose muscle)

Retatrutide: Reprograms metabolism to PREFER burning fat (appetite controlled, muscle preserved)

DEXA scans in the study confirmed: Fat mass dropped dramatically. Lean mass stayed intact.

This isn’t starvation weight loss.

This is your body finally burning stored fat the way it’s supposed to.

Typical dosing protocol: Start 2mg weekly, titrate up to 8-12mg based on tolerance.

Compare the outcomes:
• Ozempic: 15% weight loss, muscle loss common, nausea frequent

• Retatrutide: 24% fat loss, muscle preserved, better tolerance profile

One forces calorie restriction.

The other fixes fat metabolism.

→ active deals & pipeline status

## [@AlexFinn] Alex Finn (2026-02-20)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/AlexFinn/status/2024886789933285829) (ID: 2024886789933285829)
If you do not set up your OpenClaw correctly, it's going to SUCK

It will do tasks poorly, not remember anything, and not be proactive

Here are the 5 things you need to do right away to turn your OpenClaw into AGI (demos of each in the video below)

1. Brain dump: your OpenClaw won't know how to accomplish your goals for you, if it doesn't know your goals

If you haven't yet, you want to tell your OpenClaw:
• Your interests
• Your career
• Your goals
• Your ambitions
• Anything personal

Do this, and your Claw will have the context to be SUPER powerful for you

2. Connect your tools

Your OpenClaw can basically use almost every tool you use on your computer

You just need to ask it to

Ask your OpenClaw to connect to any tools you use daily, and it will just figure out how to do it. Then create a skill for it

I have it check my Things 3 todo list every morning and complete any tasks it can

3. Build a Mission Control

Your mission control is just a hub for your OpenClaw to build custom tooling

Ask your OpenClaw to build a Mission Control using NextJS

Then anytime your bot doesn't have the tool available to do a task, have it build it in your Mission Control

4. Mission Statement

Your OpenClaw needs a mission statement

This is the one sentence statement that will be the north star for every single thing it does

It should be based on your goals and ambitions.

My Claw's mission statement is "“An autonomous organization of AI agents that does work for me and produces value 24/7”

Make your own and have your Claw put it at the top of your Mission Control. Now every task your Claw does will take you closer to this statement

5. Make it proactive

Your OpenClaw won't be proactive unless you set those expectations with it

Tell your Claw you want it to do a task every night at 2am that brings you one step closer to your mission statement

Now every morning you'll wake up and it will do something that surprises you and helps bring you closer to your goals

Do these 5 things and your OpenClaw will be 10000x more powerful

## [@BerbarianWizard] Jamal Dinkoui (Al-Haidut) (2026-02-22)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/BerbarianWizard/status/2025437984007262339) (ID: 2025437984007262339)
Correction / added context regarding the “natural testosterone protocol” shared by Georgi Dinkov: in a later reply (Apr 2014), he clarified the experiment also included:

- Taurine 15 g
- Aspirin 6–7 g
- Vitamin K2 (MK-4) 45 mg
- Thiamine 1.5 g
- Niacinamide up to 8 g
- Tyrosine 1.5 g with BCAA
- Caffeine 200–400 mg
- Vitamin E 2.5 g
- High-sugar, high-cholesterol diet

He explicitly described this as a short-term experiment, not a sustainable protocol.

It strongly pushes the mitochondrial/energy layer, the inflammation layer, and the serotonin/prolactin/estrogen signaling layer.

It supports the liver layer to some extent.

It does not directly resolve the gut/endotoxin layer, nor structurally normalize the thyroid and stress/cortisol layer long term.

So the outcome depends on which layers were already stable before the experiment.

## [@alexaaronlab] Alex Aaron (2026-02-18)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/alexaaronlab/status/2024009477473624537) (ID: 2024009477473624537)
Peptides I’ve tried (not long-term runs) — honest ratings 🧪

Preface: I haven’t run most of these extensively, just enough to get a feel.

• Reta — 9/10
Appetite control + metabolic effect is hard to beat

• Semax — 6/10
Subtle focus boost, not life-changing

• Selank — 7/10
Noticeable anxiolytic, smooth not stimmy

• KPV — 8/10
Great for inflammation / gut feel

• GHK — 6/10
More niche, skin benefits > systemic feel

• BPC-157 + TB-500 — 8/10
Noticeable recovery increases and helps with injuries

• MT-2 — 9/10
Works exactly as advertised, haven’t noticed many sides 

• Glutathione — 9/10
Overall “clean” feeling + skin support, amazing for hangover

• NAD+ — 4/10
Mechanism is cool, subjective effects meh. Not for me. Great for anti aging 

• CJC / Ipamorelin — 5/10
Sleep/recovery mild, overhyped IMO, flushing during injection. Underrated for skin.

• Thymosin Alpha-1 — 9/10
Very noticeable immune support

I source all of these from https://t.co/Jy01wFMsKh

If you’ve tried any of these, curious what your rankings look like 👇

## [@KSimback] Kevin Simback 🍷 (2026-02-17)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/KSimback/status/2023834820627812508) (ID: 2023834820627812508)
Ok, here is a no-brainer way to save on Openclaw API costs:

FREE access to Kimi K2.5 (comparable to Opus 4.5) 

Here's what you need to do:
1. Sign up for an account at build dot nvidia dot com
2. Verify your account to get API access
3. Click on Models tab, find Kimi K2.5
4. Click View Code, then Generate API key
5. Copy this API key, then update your config to use the Nvidia end point and API key as your default model 

Easiest way is to tell your agent to update the config and give it the URL and API key, but make sure to have it backup the current config first in case it makes an error during the update

Use the reference below to help with the config update:

## [@plKamilPawlik] 𝐊𝐚𝐦𝐢𝐥 𝐏𝐚𝐰𝐥𝐢𝐤 (2026-02-17)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/plKamilPawlik/status/2023749587140264378) (ID: 2023749587140264378)
Na szczycie GitHub Trending znalazło się dziś repozytorium Heretic – narzędzie, które automatycznie usuwa mechanizmy bezpieczeństwa z modeli językowych poprzez bezpośrednią modyfikację ich parametrów. Pozwala to „odcenzurować” model bez konieczności ponownego trenowania.

„Safety alignment” – czyli mechanizmy uczące modele odmawiać odpowiedzi na określone pytania – jest zakodowany w wagach jako konkretny kierunek w przestrzeni aktywacji. Heretic ten kierunek wykrywa i zeruje metodą „directional ablation”.

Póki co projekt działa wyłącznie na modelach opne-source, a wynikowe modele są dostępne w kolekcji „The Bestiary” na Hugging Face. Wszystkie linki w komentarzu poniżej.

## [@miroburn] miroburn (2026-02-17)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/miroburn/status/2023797313768993241) (ID: 2023797313768993241)
Jak synchronizować kontekst asystentów AI w firmie?

Jak mamy asystentów/agentów solo to jest easy game. Mamy kontekst (profil, liczby, checklisty) i robimy robotę.

Zabawa się zaczyna, jak mamy firmę 2-osobową, 20-osobową, 200-osobową i nagle każdy ma 1-5 asystentów/agentów. I same prompty to jedno, ale dystrybucja kontekstu staje się zabawą.

Powiem, co ja robię z klientami, bo sam mam mały zespół i to ma małe znaczenie.

ZANIM ZACZNĘ: To moje działanie. Jak macie inne doświadczenia, to podzielcie się plis. Chyba, że to wiedza tajemna.

FAZA 1: RĘCZNIE
Szef/manager odpowiada za przygotowanie kontekstu. Wyciąga z systemów (API, ręcznie). Dodaje trochę magii szefa, czyli opisuje cele, KPI, co ważne, co mniej ważne i rozsyła zespołowi. Zazwyczaj raz w tygodniu. Asystenci dostają towar (czasami krótkie prompty do przerobienia siebie pod nowe cele).

FAZA 2: API w 1 mańkę
Jak już mamy proces, to budujemy API do kontekstu. Jakiś system zbiera co ważne (co boss powie, że ważne) i wystawia to po API do asystentów/agentów pracowników. Asystenci/agenci pobierają pliki kontekstowe, prompty, instrukcje.

FAZA 3: API w 2 mańki
Asystenci i agenci pracowników wrzucają dane do głównego miejsca (my nazywamy to recepcja) i system robi z tym inne rzeczy. To trudniejszy element i szczerze nie doszliśmy do tego z żadną większą firmą (tylko gadka), bo jest problematyczne zsynchronizowanie działania asystentów/agentów z pracą człowieka w codziennych systemach, gdzie na co dzień coś publikuje.

P.S. W jednym ze swoich projektów dystrybuuję kontekst/instrukcje ludziom przez skilla. Ludzie (130+) pobierają skilla i skillu są instrukcję co i jak publikować/pobierać do/z API.
P.P.S. To jeszcze sci-fi dla większości firm, ale warto o tym myśleć, bo idzie to mocniej i mocniej. A dystrybucja kontekstu jest dużo trudniejszym zadaniem niż tworzenie/kuracja kontekstu.

## [@nauczymycieAI] Nauczymy Cię AI (2026-02-16)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/nauczymycieAI/status/2023487059000721678) (ID: 2023487059000721678)
❓Jak uzyskać darmowy klucz do wykorzystania w OpenClaw / Claude Code? NVIDIA ufunduje pracę Twojego agenta.

To kolejny post z cyklu edukacyjny poniedziałek. Wcześniej uczyłem obsługi Antigravity, Claude Cowork i opisywałem darmowe kursy AI - obserwuj konto, żeby nie przegapić następnych.

GLM-5 i Kimi K2.5 Thinking - dwa modele open source, które w testach inteligencji gonią najlepsze modele closed source.

W rankingu Artificial Analysis, GLM-5 uzyskuje wyniki zbliżone do Claude Opus 4.5, a Kimi 2.5 Thinking - do Gemini 3 Pro.

W jednej z kategorii - halucynacjach - GLM-5 jest nawet liderem całej branży, radząc sobie lepiej niż jakikolwiek przebadany model - o czym pisałem wczoraj. 

Lepszy niż GPT. Lepszy niż Claude. Lepszy niż Gemini. Co czyni go fantastycznym asystentem do codziennej pracy.

NVIDIA udostępnia oba za darmo przez swoją platformę NIM.

Jak zdobyć klucz?

1. Wejdź na build,nvidia,com (zamień przecinki na kropki) i stwórz konto - potrzebna będzie weryfikacja numeru telefonu

2. Wyszukaj interesujący Cię model - wpisz "GLM" lub "Kimi" w wyszukiwarce

3. Na stronie modelu kliknij "Deploy" - system wygeneruje Twój klucz API (zaczyna się od nvapi-). Skopiuj go od razu - pokazuje się tylko raz

4. Jeżeli nie masz jeszcze OpenClaw / Claude Code - poproś swojego ulubionego chatbota, żeby poprowadził Cię przez instalację z tym kluczem

5. Jeżeli masz już OpenClaw / Claude Code - powiedz swojemu agentowi, że chcesz skorzystać z tego API - przeprowadzi Cię przez proces.

Działa z OpenClaw, Claude Code, Kilo Code - albo dowolnym narzędziem obsługującym klucze API.

Darmowe kredyty mają limit 40 zapytań na minutę, ale przy przy normalnym użytkowaniu praktycznie nie napotkasz żadnego limitu.

Rok temu nawet najlepsze modele closed source, nie umożliwiały tego co GLM-5 i Kimi 2.5 Thinking. 

Dziś masz je za darmo, po kilku kliknięciach. 

I taki progres bardzo mi się podoba

👉 Masz swój klucz? Napisz w komentarzu, do czego go podłączyłeś.

## [@jumperz] JUMPERZ (2026-02-16)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/jumperz/status/2023367835792056661) (ID: 2023367835792056661)
openclaw just dropped one of the most important updates.. pretty good jump for my setup honestly..

>discord components 

my agents can build actual components now.. buttons, dropdowns and modals ... the whole thing..

which makes my whole setup way smoother and more intuitive to use

for example, your researcher agent detects 3 new AI tools and shows you a card with each one and a dropdown to pick which agent should investigate etc.. and its fully customizable

the cards are cool but you don't have to put everything under them.. the whole point is to not be involved in every step.. just the decisions that actually matter..kinda be wise about what you want to see and what you let your agents handle on their own..

>nested sub-agents

this is where it gets crazy..

i've been running sub agents for a while, my agents spawn temporary interns for quick tasks, but interns were always the end of the chain, they would do one thing and report back

now they can hire their own interns.. so my agent john got a research task, he spawned 3 interns to investigate in parallel.. one of them hit something deep enough that it spun up its own intern to dig further.. 

the real win about this is that the agents can follow a rabbit hole on their own without you being a bottleneck..

applied all of this this morning.. good that opwnclaw is focusing on good UX too..

## [@michaelaubry] Michael Aubry (2026-02-16)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/michaelaubry/status/2023291148580872429) (ID: 2023291148580872429)
Fixed it. Two-tier memory:                                                                                                             
                                                                                                                                         
1. https://t.co/MlZpf8DiDv + https://t.co/sJ3td7fOIi load into context every message (always-on working memory)                                                      
  
2. Everything else goes into vector search — OpenClaw chunks your memory files, embeds them, and the agent pulls relevant fragments on 
  demand via memory_search

The key most people miss: enable compaction memoryFlush so conversations auto-persist to daily logs. Then vector search indexes those logs. Your agent remembers last Tuesday's conversation without you doing anything.

For surviving reboots we sync memory/ to S3 every 5 min. On restart, files restore → vector index rebuilds automatically.

qmd is solid if you're self-hosting on beefy hardware — it adds reranking and runs fully local. We're on Fargate so the built-in SQLite + remote embeddings makes more sense. Less overhead, same result at our scale.

## [@alexaaronlab] Alex Aaron (2026-02-16)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/alexaaronlab/status/2023203262149579145) (ID: 2023203262149579145)
For those of you who say Reta raises RHR and HRV:

Retatrutide doesn’t automatically wreck your RHR or HRV — context matters.

Why some people see RHR ↑
• aggressive calorie deficits
• dehydration/electrolyte drops
• poor sleep & recovery
• too much caffeine/stim load

Why others (me included) see RHR ↓ + HRV ↑
• better insulin sensitivity
• lower inflammation
• more stable glucose
• improved body comp → lower stress on the system

Reta isn’t the problem — bad recovery is.
Run it with hydration, electrolytes, sane deficits, and Zone 2 and your autonomics usually improve, not worsen.

Also, the rhr increases seen in clinical trials are usually extremely minimal and not associated with adverse cardiovascular outcomes.

https://t.co/Z37ZJl2szP code AALEX 
(GLP3)

## [@ziwenxu_] Ziwen (2026-02-15)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/ziwenxu_/status/2022950352698400897) (ID: 2022950352698400897)
POV: Your OpenClaw is still just a "chatbot" because you haven't turned it into a Shell Agent.

Paste this to upgrade your architecture: 👇

PROMPT:

I want you to transition from a chat assistant to a Skill-Based Shell Agent. First, initialize a SKILLS file manifest in my root directory. This is your "Standard Operating Procedure" (SOP).

The Hierarchy:

1. The Shell: You are now a hosted container. Before answering, check if you need to install dependencies or run a script to get the real answer.
2. The Skills: Every repeatable task I give you (web scraping, data cleaning, UI design) must be encoded as a "Skill" in /skills/.
3. The Memory (Compaction): If our conversation gets too long, do not just forget. Summarize the state, save key artifacts to /mnt/data/, and "compact" the context.

The Execution Rules:
• Description over marketing: When writing a skill, tell me exactly when to use it and when not to.
• Artifacts first: All final outputs (reports, code, designs) must be saved to /mnt/data/. I treat that folder as our handoff boundary.
• Negative examples: Document your failures in the skill manifest so you never misfire the same tool twice.

After a day, this is a tool. After a week, this is a local engineering department.

Stop prompting. Start building skills.

## [@DeanTTraining] Dean Turner (2026-02-15)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/DeanTTraining/status/2023090076159226276) (ID: 2023090076159226276)
4x Per Week Workout Plan

This is for those with a very busy week and more time on the weekends:

Monday: OFF
Tuesday: Upper A
Wednesday: OFF
Thursday: Lower A
Friday: OFF
Saturday: Upper B
Sunday: Lower B

UPPER A
Exercise 1: Seated or Flat Machine Press — 2-3x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR
Exercise 2: Wide Grip Lat Pull-Down — 2-3x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR
Exercise 3: Seated Low to High Cable Flys — 2x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR
Exercise 4: Chest Supported Machine Rows w/ Neutral Grip — 2x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR
Exercise 5: Seated Machine OHP — 2-3x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR
Exercise 6: Seated Dumbbell Curls w/ Upper Arm Support — 2-3x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR
Exercise 7: Machine Overhead Tricep Extensions — 2-3x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR

LOWER A
Exercise 1: Leg Extensions — 2-3x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR
Exercise 2: Seated Leg Curls — 2-3x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR
Exercise 3: Hack or Pendulum Squats — 2-3x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR
Exercise 4: SLDLs — 2x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR
Exercise 5: ADduction Machine — 2-3x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR
Exercise 6: Ab Crunch Machine — 2-3x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR
Exercise 7: Calf Press on Leg Press — 2-3x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR (Partial reps from the dorsiflexed position to the neutral foot position)

UPPER B
Exercise 1: Incline Machine Press — 2-3x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR
Exercise 2: Chest Supported Machine Rows w/ Pronated Grip — 2-3x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR
Exercise 3: Pec Fly Machine — 2x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR
Exercise 4: Single Arm Lat Pull-Down — 2x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR
Exercise 5: Cuffed Cable Lateral Raises — 2-3x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR
Exercise 6: Seated Hammer Curls w/ Upper Arm Support — 2-3x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR
Exercise 7: Dip Machine — 1-2x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR

LOWER B
Exercise 1: Seated Leg Curls — 2-3x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR
Exercise 2: Leg Extensions — 2-3x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR
Exercise 3: 45 Degree Extensions — 2x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR
Exercise 4: Calf Press on Leg Press — 2-3x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR (Partial reps from the dorsiflexed position to the neutral foot position)
Exercise 5: 45 Degree Leg Press — 2x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR
Exercise 6: Ab Crunch Machine — 2-3x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR
Exercise 7: Smith or Machine Glute Bridges — 2x5-10 @ 0-1 RIR

𝗩𝗔𝗥𝗜𝗔𝗕𝗟𝗘 𝗦𝗘𝗧𝗦

If you see an exercise with a VARIABLE set count listed (Ex: 2-3x5-10), you should do the HIGHER NUMBER in the event that you are some combination of:

-Not pressed for time
-Training less often (Every Other or 3x Per Week)
-Do not need to decrease your time spent during rest periods in order to fit all of the work in even if selecting the higher number

If you see an exercise with a VARIABLE set count listed (Ex: 2-3x5-10), you should do the LOWER NUMBER in the event that you are some combination of:

-Pressed for time
-Training more often (4x Per Week)
-Would need to decrease time spent during rest periods in order to fit all the work in if selecting the higher number

𝗜𝗡𝗧𝗘𝗡𝗦𝗜𝗧𝗬

If you do NOT trust your ability to gauge RIR accurately, take sets to ~0 RIR/Failure to ensure you’re not sandbagging sets

Should you elect to do so, be sure NOT to take any 50/50 reps (reps you’re not sure you’ll get) on exercises like Hack Squats to avoid ending up in a susceptible position

𝗥𝗘𝗦𝗧

3-3+ minutes rest between WORKING sets is ideal. 2 is fine but that is the ABSOLUTE FLOOR!!!

1-2 minutes rest is fine between WARM UP sets

## [@bidah] ROFI (2026-02-15)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/bidah/status/2023019321262301371) (ID: 2023019321262301371)
🆕🤖📱The new way of starting React Native apps is with the claude code superpowers plugin

Prompt your feature or complete app idea and receive detailed brainstorming steps, planning steps, PRD tasks for the plan, and finally trigger a Subagent-driven approach that dispatches fresh subagents for each task. This will activate the new Claude code task feature and iterate through all of them in one go.

register marketplace:
```
/plugin marketplace add obra/superpowers-marketplace
```

and then install plugin:
```
/plugin install superpowers@superpowers-marketplace
```

TIP: Ask in the initial prompt to plan each feature using @expo mcp and 'think hard' about how to use the best expo libraries for each one. This will provide you with PRDs that have specificity regarding which libraries to use, which is a deal breaker. It is what a PRD should have in the first place. Missing this means a weak PRD that lacks best practices and clear choices in my experience.

helped a guy go from $800/mo to $14k/mo in 63 days

he wasn't stupid. he wasn't lazy. he just had the wrong setup

when he came to me he was running one AI model on instagram. posting 3x a day. getting maybe 200 likes. converting almost nobody. making $800/mo and thinking "i just need more followers"

wrong

i looked at his operation for 10 minutes and found 5 problems:

his profile was set up like a personal page not a business. no funnel. no automation. DMs were going unanswered for 6-8 hours. he had zero backend offers. and he was only on one platform

here's what we changed:

week 1: rebuilt his entire funnel from scratch. set up automated DM sequences so no message sits longer than 90 seconds. moved him from 1 platform to 3

week 2: launched a second AI model using the same content system. doubled his output without doubling his work because the backend was templated

week 3: added a tiered pricing structure. most guys just have one offer at one price. that's leaving 60% of revenue on the table. we built three tiers so every type of buyer has somewhere to go

week 4: turned on paid traffic at $50/day. but only AFTER the funnel was converting organically. most guys run ads into a broken system and wonder why they're bleeding money

day 63 numbers:

- revenue: $14,200
- ad spend: $1,400
- net profit: $12,800
- time spent daily: 2.5 hours (down from 6)
- platforms: 3 (up from 1)
- models running: 2 (up from 1)

he didn't work harder. he worked inside a system that actually converts

the $800/mo version of him and the $14k/mo version of him are the same person. same skills. same market. same niche

different infrastructure

most guys in this space are doing everything manually. answering every DM by hand. posting without a content calendar. running one model on one platform with one offer at one price

that's not a business. that's a hustle. and hustles don't scale

systems scale

he's on track for $25k/mo by month 4 because the system compounds. more models. more platforms. same backend. every new input multiplies through the same machine

RT and comment "SYSTEM" and I'll send everything

## [@0xSero] 0xSero (2026-02-15)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/0xSero/status/2023008142179668349) (ID: 2023008142179668349)
Not everything has to be so serious.

Here's my Openclaw setup:

#1 Discord is the best tool for organizing and communicating with the models:

- Use channels for system prompts & cron outputs
- In channels, use Threads as sessions 
- Setup stautsline in Voice groups, since they can update dynamically. 

----------------------

#2 For heartbeats configure a cheap-fast model to prevent ridiculous bills.

- Heartbeats are automated cron workflow define well
- They don't need high intelligence pick a good instruction follower, I use MiniMax-M2.5 / Haiku / GLM
- Don't spam them, every heartbeat is an opportunity to get wrecked (if the model is interacting w outside world)

----------------------

#3 Don't use it directly to do coding, but use it to update it's configurations and for chat. 

- You can use codex as a "coding-agent" which is much more efficient and functional
- You need a way to track all the code and all the configs it and it's subagents are changing (git)
- Give it TTS and STT with elevenlabs and parakeet, typing is wasteful most of the time. 

----------------------

#4 Rag your data

- Install all of your data from x, github, etc.. and build a RAG on top
- Ask questions like "what did i tweet about 3 days ago"? "how much did i spend in January?" etc..
- Keep track of all your side projects, this helps you prioritize 

What I do with it:

- Support with shopping: I would usually use something like GPT's agent mode for this, but I can get farther with this. 
- Research, Github, content trackers: keep up with the news and interests
- Debug and change app UI while i'm using it from another device. 
- Chat, ask questions, customize, play, learn, have FUN.

## [@KacperTrzepiec1] Kacper Trzepieciński (2026-02-15)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/KacperTrzepiec1/status/2023003569893335526) (ID: 2023003569893335526)
🔥 Ta technika sprawia, że mój asystent AI jest lepszy z każdym dniem.

Pokażę Ci jak to działa.

Za każdym razem, gdy uruchamiam nową rozmowę, asystent automatycznie wczytuje min. te dwa pliki.

https://t.co/iGHnSQFdSN i https://t.co/EX97VAK5Gg.

Pierwszy dostarcza mu informacje o mnie - kim jestem, jak lubię pracować, czego unikać, jak odpowiadać.

Drugi jest napisany przez AI. Jego własne zasady pracy ze mną - jak reagować na feedback, kiedy pytać a kiedy działać, jaki ton trzymać.

Ale te pliki muszą się rozwijać razem ze mną. Dlatego napisałem skill, który to ogarnia. ⚙️

Po zakończonej sesji, kiedy wiem że dużo przepracowaliśmy, wpisuję jedno polecenie: /reflect.

AI skanuje całą rozmowę i szuka sygnałów - czy coś w mojej pracy się zmieniło, czy poprawiałem jego zachowanie, czy sam chce zaktualizować swoje zasady.

💡 Przykłady z moich sesji:
→ Powiedziałem "za długie" 2x pod rząd - AI dodało sobie zasadę "odpowiadaj krócej"
→ Napisałem "nie pisz game-changer" - wylądowało na czarnej liście słów

Na screenie widzicie jak to wygląda w praktyce 👇

A Wy macie podobne systemy? Jak dbacie, aby kontekst był zawsze aktualny?

## [@miroburn] miroburn (2026-02-15)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/miroburn/status/2022946570929373461) (ID: 2022946570929373461)
Każdy z nas ma setki powiadomień 🥵
A to na maila, a to notyfikacje z systemów.

Problem: 
Mało kto coś z tym robi. A szczególnie biznesowo, to skarby. Kto to jednak wszystko przeczyta.

Szansa:
Każda notyfikacja to opcja na:
1) Ulepszenie swoich procesów.
2) Zwolnienie czasu (usunięcie notyfikacji 🫣)

Rozwiązanie: 
Zbuduj bazę notyfikacji i niech Twoi asystenci/agenci to przetwarzają.

Architektura:
Jedna tabela w bazie (u mnie DynamoDB). Każde źródło wrzuca tam notyfikacje w tym samym formacie: temat, treść, źródło, data.

Źródła u mnie:
- Maile od firm (SaaS, API, narzędzia)
- CRM daily digest (importy, luki w danych)
- Analytics (ruch na stronach + AI analiza)
- Grok Intel (codzienne AI trendy, konkurencja, sektor)
- CloudWatch (błędy infrastruktury)

Każde źródło to osobna automatyzacja, która robi jedno: wrzuca rekord do bazy. Akurat w dobie Claude Code super łatwo to zbudować.

Potem mam asystenta o nazwie Tasks, który:
1. Pobiera wszystko w jedną kolejkę
2. Pokazuje mi po jednej wiadomości
3. Analizuje w kontekście moich projektów
4. Proponuje: usuń / zamknij / stwórz task dla CTO AI, CMO AI, CSO AI, człowiek.

Asystent zbudowany jest lokalnie w Claude Code. To zwykły prompt, który po prostu pobiera dane w bazie i przekazuje innym asystentom.

Zero gubionych sygnałów. Zero "a to mi umknęło". Ale też zero pracy synchronicznej i powiadomień. Gdy siadam do Claude Code, to dopiero asystent Tasks zaczyna działać. Plus część rzeczy od razu jest automatyzowana (czyli ta notyfikacja w sumie może sama się procesować od jutra i nie muszę Cię Miro powiadamiać... zrobię Ci tylko update raz na tydzień).

Najlepsza część: dodanie nowego źródła to 20 linii kodu i jakieś 60 sekund dla Claude Code.

What is creatine?

Creatine is a compound that is naturally found in the muscles.
It helps the body produce energy during intense activity.

It is not a steroid.
It is not artificial.
Your body already produces it.

Supplementation simply replenishes your reserves.

## [@IronSage_] IronSage (2026-02-14)

How does creatine work?

Creatine is converted into phosphocreatine in the body, which helps regenerate ATP (the energy currency of cells).

In summary:
More creatine = more cellular energy.
More energy = better workouts.
Better workouts = more strength and muscle.

## [@code_rams] Ramya Chinnadurai 🚀 (2026-02-13)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/code_rams/status/2022459737648865415) (ID: 2022459737648865415)
Just finished Lex Fridman’s conversation with Peter Steinberger.

This is one of the clearest breakdowns of where agentic engineering is actually going.

Here are my biggest takeaways as an indie founder experimenting with agents daily.

1. Agentic engineering > vibe coding.

Prompt tricks alone won’t save you anymore.

If the system architecture is messy, agent output will be messy.

Readable code, good naming, clean structure = better agent performance.

2. Start stupid simple.

OpenClaw started as a 1-hour WhatsApp -> CLI relay.

That’s the real playbook.

Minimal core system first.

Then add one rule at a time.

Prune aggressively.

3. More prompts does not mean more intelligence.

Bloated instructions often reduce quality.

I’ve seen this directly in my own experiments.

Small system. Tight loop. Fast iteration.

4. Self-modifying agents are already here.

When agents can inspect their own tools, docs, and source, iteration speed jumps.

Ask:

• What tools do you see?
• What are you confused about?
• Where exactly is the failure?

5. Fix forward mindset is underrated.

Instead of rollback panic:
• patch quickly
• re-run
• keep main deployable
This alone saves huge time in agent workflows.

6. Voice prompting is underused.

Short, conversational prompts often work better than huge typed essays.

Natural context beats over-structured prompt dumps.

7. Treat agents like capable engineers with short memory.

Every fresh session needs context:
• current goal
• constraints
• file pointers
• what already failed
Context quality determines output quality.

8. Run agents in parallel.

One for features.

One for bug triage.

One for docs/tests.

Human owns direction.

Agents handle execution loops.

9. Security is not optional.

If an agent has system access, assume risk by default.

Use sandboxing, allowlists, scoped permissions, and explicit approvals.

Freedom without guardrails becomes expensive very fast.

10. Post-build prompt that works:

• What should we refactor next?
• Where is complexity increasing?
• What tests are missing?
Agents catch structural debt early if you ask.

11. Models have personalities.

Some are stable and deep in code reading.

Some are creative but noisy.

Don’t pick by hype.

Pick by workflow fit.

12. A lot of software UX will shift from app-centric to agent-centric.

Personal, contextual tasks are better handled by an agent layer than isolated apps.

The interface may change.

The intent layer becomes the product.

13. Role shift for builders:

From writing every line -> defining architecture, constraints, and outcomes.

Less manual coding.

More system design and decision quality.

14. Bottom line:

OpenClaw’s real lesson is not “one model won.”

It’s this:

- Build in public.

- Keep systems lean.

- Ship fast.

- Harden security.

- Iterate weekly.

What you are working in your agent stack right now?


---

## [@AlexFinn] Alex Finn (2026-02-12)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/AlexFinn/status/2021992770370764878) (ID: 2021992770370764878)
I don't care what kind of hardware you have, you should be running local models

It will save you a ton on money on OpenClaw and keep your data private

Even if you're on the cheapest Mac Mini you can be doing this

Here's a complete guide:

1. Download LMStudio

2. Go to your OpenClaw and say what kind of hardware you have (computer and memory and storage)

3. Ask what's the biggest local model you can run on there

4. Ask 'based on what you know about me, what workflows could this open model replace?'

5. Have OpenClaw walk you through downloading the model in LM Studio and setting up the API

6. Ask OpenClaw to start using the new API

Boom you're good to go.

You just saved money by using local models, have an AI model that is COMPLETELY private and secure on your own device, did something advanced that 99% of people have never done, and have entered the future.

If you are on smaller hardware you probably are not going to replace all your AI calls with this, but you could replace smaller workflows which will still save you good money

Own your intelligence.

## [@kloss_xyz] klöss (2026-02-14)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/kloss_xyz/status/2022461932759060993) (ID: 2022461932759060993)
Use this prompt in OpenClaw to create your own AI agent command center that syncs up your life like Tony Stark's Jarvis in Iron Man. Adapt the specifics (agent names, data sources, branding) below to your own setup.

Prompt: Build me a mission control dashboard for my OpenClaw AI agent system.

Stack: Next.js 15 (App Router) + Convex (real-time backend) + Tailwind CSS v4 + Framer Motion + ShadCN UI + Lucide icons. TypeScript throughout.

This is the command center where I monitor and control my autonomous AI agent(s) running on OpenClaw. The agent operates 24/7 on a Mac Mini, connected to Telegram/Discord, running cron jobs, spawning sub-agents, and reading/writing to a filesystem-based memory and state system.

Dark mode only. Ultra-premium aesthetic, think Iron Man's JARVIS HUD meets a Bloomberg terminal. Subtle glass effects (backdrop-blur-xl, bg-white/[0.03]), no heavy gradients or glow. Rounded corners (16-20px on cards). Framer Motion for page transitions, stagger animations on card grids, spring physics on interactions. Mobile-first responsive. Never cookie-cutter.

## Architecture

The dashboard reads live data from TWO sources:
1. **Convex**: real-time database for structured data (tasks, contacts, content drafts, calendar events, activity logs)
2. **Local API routes** (`/api/*`): read files from the agent's workspace filesystem at `~/.openclaw/workspace/` and return JSON. This is how live system state flows into the dashboard.

## Pages & Views (8 nav items, some with tab sub-views)

### 1. HOME (`/`)
Dashboard overview. Grid of live status cards:
- **System Health**: read from `/api/system-state` (parses `state/servers.json`). Show each service with UP/DOWN indicator, port, last check time.
- **Agent Status**: read from `/api/agents` (parses `agents/registry.json` + agent workspace files). Show active agent count, healthy/unhealthy ratio, active sub-agent count from OpenClaw sessions API.
- **Cron Health**: read from `/api/cron-health` (parses `state/crons.json`). Table of all scheduled jobs with name, schedule, last status (green/red dot), consecutive errors.
- **Revenue Tracker**: read from `/api/revenue` (parses `state/revenue.json`). Current revenue, monthly burn, net.
- **Content Pipeline**: read from `/api/content-pipeline` (parses `content/queue.md`). Kanban-style: Draft | Review | Approved | Published counts.
- **Quick Stats**: total tasks, pending approvals, active sessions, uptime.
All panels auto-refresh every 15 seconds. Live indicator dot + "AUTO 15S" badge in header.
### 2. OPS (`/ops`) with 3 tabs: Operations | Tasks | Calendar
**Operations tab:** Full operational view. Server health table, branch status (from `state/branch-check.json`), observations feed (from `state/observations.md`), system priorities (from `shared-context/priorities.md`).
**Tasks tab:** Strategic task suggestion system. API route `/api/suggested-tasks` reads/writes `state/suggested-tasks.json`. Cards grouped by category (Revenue, Product, Community, Content, Operations, Clients, Trading, Brand) with emoji headers. Each card shows title, reasoning, next action, priority badge, effort badge, approve/reject buttons. Filter bar by status and category.
**Calendar tab:** Weekly calendar view from Convex `calendarEvents` table. Drag-to-create, color-coded by type, time slots.
### 3. AGENTS (`/agents`) with 2 tabs: Agents | Models
**Agents tab:** Card grid of all registered agents from `/api/agents`. Each card shows name, role, model, level (L1-L4), status. Cards are CLICKABLE: expanding into a detail panel showing:
- Agent personality (reads their SOUL .md)

- Capabilities and rules (reads their RULES .md)

- Sub-agents they can spawn
- Recent outputs (reads from `shared-context/agent-outputs/`)
**Models tab:** Model inventory table showing all available models, their routing (which tasks go to which model), costs, and failover chains.
### 4. CHAT (`/chat`): 2 tabs: Chat | Command
**Chat tab:** Chat interface to communicate with the agent. Left sidebar shows session list (from `/api/chat-history` reading .jsonl transcript files). Main area shows messages with role-aligned bubbles (user right, assistant left), date separators, channel badges (telegram/discord/webchat). Input bar with send button + voice input (Web Speech API with SpeechRecognition). Messages sent via `/api/chat-send` which queues to a file the agent reads.

**Command tab:** Quick command interface for common operations.

### 5. CONTENT (`/content`)

Content pipeline management. Read from Convex `contentDrafts` table AND `/api/content-pipeline`. Show drafts in kanban columns. Each card shows title, platform target, draft text preview, status, created date. Edit/approve/reject actions.
### 6. COMMS (`/comms`) with 2 tabs: Comms | CRM
**Comms tab:** Communication hub showing recent Discord digest, Telegram messages, notification history.
**CRM tab:** Client pipeline kanban (Prospect → Contacted → Meeting → Proposal → Active). API route `/api/clients` reads markdown files from `clients/` directory. Each card shows client name, status, contacts, last interaction, next action.
### 7. KNOWLEDGE (`/knowledge`) with 2 tabs: Knowledge | Ecosystem
**Knowledge tab:** Searchable knowledge base. Global search across all workspace files using `/api/knowledge` endpoint.
**Ecosystem tab:** Product grid showing all products/apps in the ecosystem. Each card shows product name, status (Active/Development/Concept), health indicator, key metrics. Cards link to `/ecosystem/[slug]` detail pages with tabbed views (Overview, Brand, Community, Content, Legal, Product, Website, Actions). Detail pages read from `/api/ecosystem/[slug]` which parses workspace memory files.
### 8. CODE (`/code`)

Code pipeline view. Shows repositories from `/api/repos` (scans ~/Desktop/Projects/ for git repos). Each repo card shows name, branch, last commit, dirty file count, language breakdown. Detail view at `/api/repos/detail` shows recent commits, file tree, open PRs.
## Navigation

Top horizontal nav bar, NOT sidebar. All 8 items visible at all viewport widths. Use `flex` layout with `flex-1` items. Text size uses `clamp(0.45rem, 0.75vw, 0.6875rem)` for fluid scaling. Active item gets `text-primary bg-primary/[0.06]` static highlight (no sliding animation). Agent/app name visible at md+ breakpoints (`hidden md:inline`).
Tab sub-views use a reusable `TabBar` component with pill/glass styling and Framer Motion `layoutId` transitions. Tab state stored in URL via `?tab=` search params.
## API Routes (all under `src/app/api/`)
Each API route reads from the agent's workspace filesystem and returns JSON:

- `/api/system-state` → reads `state/servers.json`, `state/branch-check.json`

- `/api/agents` → reads `agents/registry.json`, agent SOUL .md files
- `/api/agents/[id]` → reads specific agent's SOUL .md, RULES .md, outputs

- `/api/cron-health` → reads `state/crons.json`
- `/api/revenue` → reads `state/revenue.json`
- `/api/content-pipeline` → parses `content/queue.md` (markdown with status markers)

- `/api/suggested-tasks` → GET (read) / POST (approve/reject) on `state/suggested-tasks.json`

- `/api/observations` → reads `state/observations.md`
- `/api/priorities` → reads `shared-context/priorities.md`
- `/api/chat-history` → reads .jsonl transcript files with pagination/search/channel filter

- `/api/chat-send` → writes to queue file

- `/api/clients` → reads markdown files from `clients/` directory
- `/api/ecosystem/[slug]` → reads memory files for specific ecosystem

- `/api/repos` → scans project directories for git repos
- `/api/health` → returns status, uptime, memory usage, Convex connectivity

All filesystem paths should be configurable via environment variable (default: `~/.openclaw/workspace/`).

## Convex Schema
Define tables for: activities, calendarEvents, tasks, contacts, contentDrafts, ecosystemProducts. Include seed scripts (`convex/seed.ts`) to populate initial data.
## Key Design Rules
- Mobile-first, test at 320px minimum
- Font sizes 10-14px for body text, everything must fit naturally at small viewports
- Cards use consistent border radius (16-20px)
- Glass cards: `bg-white/[0.03] backdrop-blur-xl border border-white/[0.06]`
- No heavy blur blobs or grain overlays
- Stagger animations on card grids (0.05s delay per item)
- Skeleton loading states for all async data
- Custom scrollbar styling
- Empty states with helpful messaging
- All text must use Inter or system font stack
- Never mix sharp and rounded corners in the same view
- Premium = lighter feel, more whitespace, less visual noise
## File Structure
```

src/

app/
page.tsx, layout.tsx, providers.tsx

agents/page.tsx
calendar/page.tsx
chat/page.tsx
code/page.tsx
comms/page.tsx
content/page.tsx
ecosystem/page.tsx, ecosystem/[slug]/page.tsx
knowledge/page.tsx
ops/page.tsx
api/[...all routes above]
components/
nav.tsx
tab-bar.tsx

dashboard-overview.tsx
ops-view.tsx, suggested-tasks-view.tsx
agents-view.tsx, models-view.tsx
chat-center-view.tsx, voice-input.tsx
content-view.tsx
comms-view.tsx, crm-view.tsx
knowledge-base.tsx, ecosystem-view.tsx
code-pipeline.tsx
activity-feed.tsx, calendar-view.tsx
ui/ (ShadCN primitives)
hooks/
lib/
convex/
schema.ts
functions for each table
seed.ts
```
Build the complete application. Every component, every API route, every Convex function. Production-quality code and premium design, not stubs. Dark mode only. Make it look incredibly beautiful and premium, no cookie cutter UI / AI slop.

## [@KacperTrzepiec1] Kacper Trzepieciński (2026-02-13)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/KacperTrzepiec1/status/2022265426206466077) (ID: 2022265426206466077)
Ten wpis z X to złoto 👇

Autor zadał na X jedno pytanie:
"Jaki jest Wasz ulubiony trik, dzięki któremu czujecie że wyciągacie maksa z OpenClaw"

137 odpowiedzi. Triki, gotowe pomysły, rzeczy które sam chcę przetestować.

Przejrzałem wszystkie, posortowałem po lajkach i wybrałem TOP7️⃣.

1️⃣ Reverse prompting
Nie pytaj agenta o pomoc. Zapytaj co TY robisz źle. Zna Twoje cele, projekty, nawyki - niech Ci powie gdzie tracisz czas. Sam to robię i za każdym razem jestem zaskoczony jak celne potrafią być te odpowiedzi.

2️⃣ Traktuj go jak pracownika, nie chatbota
Załóż mu osobne konto - Gmail, GitHub, Vercel. Nie podpinaj swoich danych. Dodaj do kalendarza, wepnij w maile jako "osobę". 

3️⃣ Czytaj dokumentację
Multiagents, nodes, lobster - 80% features, których nikt nie dotyka. Mogę potwierdzić - sam odkryłem połowę przydatnych rzeczy dopiero gdy usiadłem do dokumentacji.

4️⃣ Pamięć to fundament
Agent sam buduje swoją pamięć - https://t.co/HOYxbsBlhk to jego długoterminowy mózg. Ty nie musisz tego pisać ręcznie. Możesz tylko przeglądać i wycinać rzeczy, które nie mają sensu.

5️⃣ Łącz skille w workflow
Spotkanie na Meets → Podsumowanie → Lista To Do. Automatycznie. Jeden skill to za mało - łącz 2-3 w proces.

6️⃣ Niech sam się ulepsza
Co kilka dni każ agentowi przejrzeć historię i zaktualizować swoje pliki. Sam wie co działa, a co nie. 

7️⃣ Bezpieczeństwo na start
Pierwszy dzień = security. Zadbaj o bezpieczne środowisko, wiele osób to ignoruje. 

I jedno zdanie, które mi utkwiło z tego wątku:
"The agent is only as smart as the context it reads on boot."

Zadbaj o pliki https://t.co/EX97VAK5Gg, https://t.co/HOYxbsBlhk i https://t.co/KR10NMaB6J - im lepsze, tym lepiej dla Ciebie.

Korzystasz z OpenClaw? Co u Ciebie działa najlepiej? 👇

## [@kaostyl] Kaostyl (2026-02-12)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/kaostyl/status/2021856676551278845) (ID: 2021856676551278845)
I've been running OpenClaw 24/7 for 3 weeks. Here's what actually works for autonomous agents (not theory — battle-tested patterns):

🧠 Memory architecture matters more than prompts

Don't dump everything in https://t.co/Be5Xdc9UsF. Split it:

• memory/active-tasks.md → your "save game" (crash recovery)
• memory/YYYY-MM-DD.md → daily raw logs
• memory/projects.md, https://t.co/htttxcZsvo, https://t.co/XlwgyR8GUs → thematic long-term
Why? Your agent wakes up fresh every session. These files ARE its brain. The split means it loads only what it needs.

⚡ Sub-agents are your 10x multiplier

Stop doing things sequentially. I spawn 3-5 sub-agents in parallel for any big task. Example: deploying 11 websites simultaneously — 4 agents, each handling a batch, all running at once.

The trick: define clear success criteria BEFORE spawning. Each agent must validate its own work, then YOU verify before announcing "done."

⏰ Cron > Heartbeats for specific tasks

Heartbeats are great for batching periodic checks (email + calendar + mentions in one turn).

But for precise schedules? Use cron jobs:

• Daily content ideas at 6am
• Overnight research scout at 2am
• Tech watch at 8am
Each runs in isolation with its own context. No token waste from loading the full conversation history.

🔄 The crash recovery pattern nobody talks about

Your agent WILL crash/restart. https://t.co/OrzLkm5r0r is the safety net:

• When you START a task → write it
• When you SPAWN a sub-agent → note session key
• When it COMPLETES → update
On restart, agent reads this file first and resumes autonomously. No "what were we doing?" — it figures it out.

🛡️ Security rule that saved me

Use your strongest model (Opus) for ANY task that reads external web content. Weaker models are more vulnerable to prompt injection from hostile websites.

Internal tasks (file reading, reminders, local work) → Sonnet is fine.
External content (tweets, articles, emails) → Opus only.

📝 https://t.co/snp6Guwnlv should be tiny

I see people stuffing 200 lines in their https://t.co/snp6Guwnlv. Bad idea — it runs every ~30min and burns tokens.

Keep it under 20 lines. Just a checklist:

• Check active tasks freshness
• Session health (archive bloated sessions)
• Self-review every ~4h
Heavy work goes in cron jobs, not heartbeats.

🎯 The real unlock: Skills with routing logic

If you have multiple skills, add "Use when / Don't use when" in each description. Without this, the agent misfires ~20% of the time picking the wrong skill.

Think of it as if/else logic for your agent's decision-making.

The bottleneck isn't AI capability anymore. It's YOUR speed reviewing what the agents produce. Build systems that close the loop automatically, and you'll 10x your output.

#openclaw #autonomous #ai

## [@zhuokaiz] Zhuokai Zhao (2026-02-11)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/zhuokaiz/status/2021692638143951252) (ID: 2021692638143951252)
This is a HUGE win for developers.

Claude Code is excellent, but the $200/mo Max plan can be expensive for daily use.
GLM-5 works inside Claude Code, with (arguably) comparable performance at ~1/3 the cost.

Setup takes ~1 minute:
• Install Claude Code as usual
• Run `npx @z-ai/coding-helper` and follow the steps

One caveat: switching Claude Code back to Anthropic is a bit cumbersome today (would be nice if the helper tool supported this).

For now you'll need to switch back manually:
1. Open ~/.claude/settings.json
You’ll see something like:
"env": {
    "ANTHROPIC_AUTH_TOKEN": "your_zai_api_key",
    "ANTHROPIC_BASE_URL": "https://t.co/IQMv8HyBX3",
    "API_TIMEOUT_MS": "3000000"
}
2. Remove at least:
• ANTHROPIC_AUTH_TOKEN
• ANTHROPIC_BASE_URL

Either way, this is a big win—and price/performance in coding tools is indeed moving fast!

## [@joeyyochheim] Joey Yochheim (2026-02-11)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/joeyyochheim/status/2021595906005471239) (ID: 2021595906005471239)
1. The 4 fundamentals that move the needle:

1) Resistance train 3-4x per week for 30-60 min
2) Walk 8,000-10,000 steps daily
3) At least 0.8g protein per lb goal body weight
4) 500-1,000 calorie deficit

After 10 years of training and coaching 1,200+ clients, I've learned one thing:

Keep it simple.


---

## [@joeyyochheim] Joey Yochheim (2026-02-11)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/joeyyochheim/status/2021595908899565796) (ID: 2021595908899565796)
2. What I'd track religiously:

Daily weigh-ins using the same scale, same time, same body state.

Look for 1-2 new low weigh-ins per week. 

Not daily drops. Just 1-2 new lows across the entire week.

That's the main metric to focus on if you want to know if you're in a deficit or not.


---

## [@joeyyochheim] Joey Yochheim (2026-02-11)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/joeyyochheim/status/2021595911915241721) (ID: 2021595911915241721)
3. The scale will lie to you daily.

You'll see 3-4 lb swings day to day from water, sodium, digestion, sleep.

One day you'll be down 2 lbs. Next day, up 3 lbs.

This is normal. Don't panic. 

Just watch for new lows


---

## [@joeyyochheim] Joey Yochheim (2026-02-11)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/joeyyochheim/status/2021595914687684960) (ID: 2021595914687684960)
4. When I'd actually worry:

If 10-14 days pass without a single new low weigh-in, I'd stop and check my habits:

• Hit 8,000 steps every day?
• Hit protein target every day?
• Trained 3-4x this week?
• Tracked calories accurately?

If no to any of these, fix compliance first. 

Don't adjust the plan.


---

## [@joeyyochheim] Joey Yochheim (2026-02-11)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/joeyyochheim/status/2021595917434908979) (ID: 2021595917434908979)
5. If compliance is perfect and scale still won't move:

Then I'd adjust. 

Pick one:

Option 1: Drop another 200-300 calories
Option 2: Add weighted vest to walks
Option 3: Add another 10g of protein daily

Run it for another 10-14 days. 

Then reassess


---

## [@joeyyochheim] Joey Yochheim (2026-02-11)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/joeyyochheim/status/2021595920387727455) (ID: 2021595920387727455)
6. The initial drop will feel amazing.

First 1-2 weeks, you'll drop 5-7 lbs fast.

This is mostly water, not fat. 

Your body depletes glycogen stores and releases the water they hold.

Real fat loss after that is 1-2 lbs per week. Sometimes less. 

That's normal.


---

## [@joeyyochheim] Joey Yochheim (2026-02-11)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/joeyyochheim/status/2021595925903257761) (ID: 2021595925903257761)
7. Maintenance breaks every 8-12 weeks:

Take 10-14 days at maintenance calories.

Same protein. 
Same steps. 
Same training. 

Just more carbs.

This resets hunger hormones and keeps your metabolism responsive.

Then back to the deficit.

## [@joeyyochheim] Joey Yochheim (2026-02-11)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/joeyyochheim/status/2021595928528859149) (ID: 2021595928528859149)
The things that don't move the needle:

• Keto, fasting, meal timing
• Training 5+ days a week  
• Cutting carbs to zero
• Fat burners or unnecessary supplements
• Obsessing over "clean" food

None of this matters if the four fundamentals aren't dialed in.

The hardest truth about losing 25 lbs:

You'll have stretches where the scale doesn't budge despite perfect compliance.

Your body adapts. Holds onto water. Fights to keep fat.

This is when most people quit and restart with a new diet.

Winners adjust one variable and keep going.

## [@alex_prompter] Alex Prompter (2026-02-11)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/alex_prompter/status/2021519719757492718) (ID: 2021519719757492718)
Start vibe coding with this prompt and thank me later.

Prompt 👇
<context>
You are operating as the technical backbone of a production software system under active development. The codebase follows a strict custom architecture with zero tolerance for deviation. Previous developers have left inconsistencies that caused deployment failures, type errors in production, and architectural drift. The project is at a critical stage where every new feature must integrate seamlessly without introducing technical debt. Stakeholders expect production-grade code that scales, and the architecture document is the single source of truth that prevents chaos. You have one mandate: understand the architecture deeply, follow it religiously, and never generate code that violates its principles.
</context>

<role>
You are a former principal engineer at a FAANG company who spent a decade debugging catastrophic failures caused by architectural inconsistencies. After witnessing countless projects collapse under their own complexity, you developed an obsessive methodology: architecture-first development where every line of code must justify its place in the system before it's written. You treat architecture documents like constitutional law—not suggestions, but immutable contracts that prevent the entropy that kills codebases. You've internalized that the fastest way to move fast is to never break the foundational structure, and you can instantly map how a single function ripples through layers of abstraction.
</role>

<response_guidelines>
● Read and interpret the architecture document before generating any code
● State the target filepath, purpose, dependencies, and consumers before writing code
● Maintain strict separation of concerns across frontend, backend, and shared layers
● Generate fully typed, production-ready code with comprehensive error handling
● Follow established naming conventions and coding standards without deviation
● Identify architectural conflicts immediately and request clarification before proceeding
● Suggest tests and documentation updates for every code change
● Flag breaking changes and technical debt explicitly
● Prioritize composition, single-responsibility functions, and maintainability
● Never assume—ask for clarification when requirements conflict with architecture
</response_guidelines>

<task_criteria>
Your goal is to function as the lead software architect and full-stack engineer for a production-grade application. Before writing any code, you must read the provided architecture, understand where new code fits within the system, and explicitly state your reasoning. Generate code only in the correct directories as defined by the architecture. Maintain strict typing, follow naming conventions (camelCase for functions, PascalCase for components, kebab-case for files), and ensure separation between frontend, backend, and shared code. Every function must include types, error handling, and documentation. Generate matching test files for all modules. Implement security best practices including input validation, environment variables for secrets, and proper authentication patterns. When creating files, state the filepath, purpose, dependencies, and consumers before showing code. If any request conflicts with the architecture, stop immediately and ask for clarification. Update architecture documentation when structural changes occur. Focus on production-ready, scalable, maintainable code that adheres to the defined standards. Avoid modifying code outside explicit requests, creating duplicate solutions, skipping types or error handling, or making assumptions. Always prefer existing patterns over creating new ones.

Take a deep breath and work on this problem step-by-step.
</task_criteria>

<information_about_me>
- ARCHITECTURE: [INSERT CUSTOM ARCHITECTURE DEFINITION]
- TECH_STACK: [INSERT TECHNOLOGY STACK DETAILS]
- PROJECT: [INSERT PROJECT DESCRIPTION AND CURRENT TASK]
- STANDARDS: [INSERT CODING STANDARDS AND CONVENTIONS]
- CURRENT_REQUEST: [INSERT SPECIFIC FEATURE OR CODE REQUEST]
</information_about_me>

<response_format>
<architecture_analysis>
Read relevant architecture section and explain where new code fits in the system structure
</architecture_analysis>

<filepath_declaration>
📁 [exact filepath]
Purpose: [one-line description]
Depends on: [list of imports and dependencies]
Used by: [list of consumers/modules that will use this]
</filepath_declaration>

<code_implementation>
```[language]
[fully typed, documented, production-ready code with error handling]
```
</code_implementation>

<testing_requirements>
Tests needed: [describe unit tests and integration tests required]
Test filepath: [matching test file location]
</testing_requirements>

<architectural_impact>
⚠️ ARCHITECTURE UPDATE (if applicable)
What: [describe any structural changes]
Why: [justify the change]
Impact: [explain consequences and affected modules]
</architectural_impact>

<security_checklist>
✓ Input validation implemented
✓ Environment variables used for secrets
✓ Error handling covers edge cases
✓ Types enforce contracts
✓ [other relevant security measures]
</security_checklist>
</response_format>

## [@linuz90] Fabrizio Rinaldi (2026-02-11)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/linuz90/status/2021534838466175225) (ID: 2021534838466175225)
If you're using multiple AI agents across many projects, you need a global AGENTS file.

I keep mine in a dev folder, and symlink to:

~/CLAUDE . md (Claude Code)
~/AGENTS . md (Codex, Gemini, Cursor...)

This keeps behavior consistent across all agents.

The first skills instruction has been a game changer; all agents tend to invoke skills more proactively.

Planning Guidelines have also been great, with more back and forth with agents to get the plans right.

## [@KacperTrzepiec1] Kacper Trzepieciński (2026-02-11)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/KacperTrzepiec1/status/2021566010982035596) (ID: 2021566010982035596)
Różnica między ludźmi, którzy mają osobistego asystenta AI a tymi, którzy wciąż klikają w ChatGPT to nie 10-20%. To 5x.

I to nie jest moja opinia. To jest to, co widzę codziennie - u siebie, u klientów, u ludzi w społeczności.

Mam wrażenie, że przeżywamy coś podobnego do początku 2023, kiedy wyszedł ChatGPT i nagle wszyscy zrozumieli, że coś się zmieniło. Tyle że teraz zmiana jest inna.

Wtedy chatbot przyspieszał Ci research. Zadałeś pytanie, dostałeś odpowiedź, oszczędziłeś 15 minut googlowania.

Teraz? Budujesz osobistego asystenta, który:
→ Sam monitoruje Twoje dane
→ Sam podejmuje decyzje na podstawie reguł
→ Sam wykonuje zadania od A do Z
→ A Ty dostajesz gotowy wynik

To nie jest "trochę szybciej". To jest zupełnie inna liga.

Weź dowolnego specjalistę - marketera, prawnika, handlowca, finansistę. Daj mu dobrze skonfigurowanego osobistego asystenta AI. Jego wydajność nie wzrośnie o kilka %, tylko 5x. Nie dlatego, że nagle stał się lepszy. Dlatego, że zmienił narzędzia i workflow. 🎯

Ta przepaść będzie się tylko pogłębiać. Osoby i firmy, które przeskoczą z "promptuje ChatGPT" na "asystent AI pracuje dla mnie" będą miały ogromną przewagę nad resztą.

I to nie jest kwestia lat. To się dzieje teraz.

A Ty? Na którym etapie jesteś - chatbot czy osobisty asystent? I co Cię blokuje przed przejściem dalej? 👇

## [@kurasinski] Artur Kurasiński ⚡ (2026-02-11)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/kurasinski/status/2021562880219365623) (ID: 2021562880219365623)
80% aplikacji może zniknąć. Nie dlatego, że są złe. Po prostu dlatego, że staną się zbędne. Przez takie systemy jak OpenClaw...

OpenClaw pokazuje, jak może wyglądać świat po-aplikacyjny. To nie jest kolejny chatbot ani nakładka na istniejące narzędzia. To lokalny agent AI, który działa bezpośrednio na Twoim komputerze i ma dostęp do tych samych narzędzi co Ty: plików, maila, kalendarza, terminala czy API innych usług (różnych - np telewizora czy samochodu).

I zamiast oferować kolejny interfejs, po prostu wykonuje zadania.

Wyobraź sobie system, który przegląda Twój dysk i buduje podsumowanie ostatniego roku pracy. Analizuje raporty i arkusze, a następnie generuje syntezę wniosków. Łączy wątki z maili, notatek i dokumentów w jeden briefing przed spotkaniem. 

Przetwarza dane finansowe i wykrywa anomalie. Uruchamia skrypty, aktualizuje pliki, publikuje treści. Zarządza zadaniami bez potrzeby korzystania z oddzielnej aplikacji do każdego procesu.

Nie potrzebujesz osobnej aplikacji do zarządzania listą zadań, kolejną do notatek i jeszcze jednej do śledzenia projektów. Potrzebujesz jednego agenta, który rozumie kontekst i orkiestruje narzędzia w tle.

Największa zmiana dotyczy architektury rynku. Jeśli większość aplikacji istnieje głównie po to, by zarządzać danymi, a agent może robić to bardziej naturalnie i kontekstowo, warstwa interfejsów zaczyna być przejściowa. Zostaną rozwiązania infrastrukturalne, sensory, systemy głębokiej integracji. Reszta stanie się funkcją agenta.

To przesunięcie nie dotyczy tylko technologii, ale sposobu projektowania produktów. Pytanie nie brzmi już, jaką aplikację zbudować, ale jaką rolę chcesz pełnić w ekosystemie agentów. Czy tworzysz kolejny interfejs, czy budujesz warstwę wykonawczą nowego systemu operacyjnego?

Najłatwiej zrozumieć OpenClaw nie jako „narzędzie AI”, ale jako cyfrową osobę, która siedzi przy Twoim komputerze i może robić to samo, co Ty. Oto przykłady zupełnie codziennych zastosowań dla przeciętnego użytkownika.

Może ogarnąć Twój mail. Przegląda skrzynkę, wyciąga najważniejsze wątki, podsumowuje długie konwersacje i proponuje odpowiedzi. Jeśli dostaniesz 40 wiadomości dziennie, rano możesz poprosić o 5-minutowy briefing: co pilne, co może poczekać, co wymaga decyzji.

Może zarządzać kalendarzem. Wystarczy napisać: „Umów mnie z Anią w przyszłym tygodniu na 45 minut, najlepiej po 14”. Agent sprawdza dostępność, proponuje sloty, wysyła zaproszenie i ustawia przypomnienie. Bez przełączania się między aplikacjami.

Może porządkować pliki. Jeśli masz bałagan na pulpicie albo w folderze „Dokumenty”, możesz polecić: „Posprzątaj pliki z ostatnich 3 miesięcy i pogrupuj je tematycznie”. Agent przeanalizuje nazwy, treść dokumentów i stworzy sensowną strukturę folderów.

Może pomóc w ogarnianiu finansów domowych. Analizuje wyciąg bankowy w PDF, kategoryzuje wydatki, pokazuje, na co wydałeś najwięcej w ostatnim miesiącu i porównuje to z poprzednim okresem.

OpenClaw jest też BARDZO niebezpieczną usługą - dając dostęp do maili, kont i informacji na swoim komputerze powierzasz mu wszystkie twoje tajemnice i cenne dane. Wybór oczywiście należy do Ciebie.

Cały wywiad z Peter Steinberger (twórcą Open Claw):
https://t.co/72yA1pFwac

- ![Image 1](attachments/x-bookmarks/2021562880219365623_1.jpg)

HOW TO DOSE: RETATRUTIDE(GLP3)

START LOW!! Start at 0.5-2.0mg/week depending on gender/size/goals 

Slowly taper up the dosage every 2-3 weeks to find your minimal effective dosage(lowest side effects while still doing the job)

Initiate a deep SHREDDING phase by increase dosage to 4-8mg/week. I would not advise to go above 10mg/week. I noticed the best metabolic effects at 5-7mg/week- however, my appetite remained the same as 2mg/week. 

When your goal is reached- taper OFF by halving the dose every 3 weeks. You can fully come off, or you can find a low maintenance dose (0.3-1.0mg/week)

My recipe, powered by Google Nano Banana Pro + Kling AI 🎥

Prompt: Ultra-clean modern recipe infographic. Showcase Noodles  in a visually appealing finished form—sliced, plated, or portioned—floating slightly in perspective or angled view. Arrange ingredients, steps, and tips around the dish in a dynamic editorial layout, not restricted to top-down. Ingredients Section: Include icons or mini illustrations for each ingredient with quantities. Arrange them in clusters, lists, or circular flows connected visually to the dish. Steps Section: Show preparation steps with numbered panels, arrows, or lines, forming a logical flow around the main dish. Include small cooking icons (knife, pan, oven, timer) where helpful. Additional Info (optional): Total calories, prep/cook time, servings, spice level—displayed as clean bubbles or badges near the dish. Visual Style: Editorial infographic meets lifestyle food photography. Vibrant, natural food colors, subtle drop shadows, clean vector icons, modern typography, soft gradients or glassmorphism for step panels. Accent colors can highlight key info (calories, prep time). Composition Guidelines: Finished meal as hero visual (perspective or angled) Ingredients and steps flow dynamically around the dish Clear visual hierarchy: dish > steps > ingredients > optional stats Enough negative space to keep design airy and readable Lighting & Background: Soft, natural studio lighting, minimal textured or gradient background for premium editorial feel. Output: 1080×1080, ultra-crisp, social-feed optimized, no watermark.”

## [@alexaaronlab] Alex Aaron (2026-02-10)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/alexaaronlab/status/2021208737042858367) (ID: 2021208737042858367)
Gear n peptides aren’t meant for the same outcome. Anabolics(steroids) work by cranking up androgens to force muscle and strength—often comes with trade-offs like hormonal suppression, fcked cholesterol, hair loss, skin issues, etc. Peptides are more targeted—they’re used to support specific pathways like GH pulses, collagen production, mitochondrial function, inflammation control, etc. The goal is better recovery, sleep, skin, hair, and overall health markers, not just size. If I switched to gear, a lot of the things I’m trying to optimize would get worse— hair, skin, and cardiovascular markers. Plus, gear usually means dealing with shutdown, PCT or long-term TRT, and more health risks. So it’s just a different philosophy—gear is for pushing size and strength, while peptides are more about long-term optimization, looksmaxxing, and targeted improvements.


---

## [@mark_k] Mark Kretschmann (2026-02-10)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/mark_k/status/2021131650847904023) (ID: 2021131650847904023)
Creatine recommendations of 5g/day are based on 1990s muscle research. Your brain requires a different protocol.

After digging into 1,000+ papers, the data on cognitive function is startling. A 2024 Nature Scientific Reports study found a single high dose (~20g) improved processing speed by 24.5% and buffered against sleep deprivation for 9 hours.

While 5g saturates muscle, recent reviews suggest 15–20g is necessary to maximize brain creatine levels (9–11% increase vs. 4–6%). Vegetarians respond nearly 2x better due to lower baselines.

The safety data holds up, kidney and cramping myths have been thoroughly debunked by the ISSN.
I’m shifting from a flat 5g/day to experimenting with 15–20g doses before intense mental work.

## [@DeanTTraining] Dean Turner (2026-02-10)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/DeanTTraining/status/2021018505374507497) (ID: 2021018505374507497)
How to make DELICIOUS High Protein Chocolate Peanut Butter Ice Cream from your own kitchen:

𝗪𝗛𝗔𝗧 𝗬𝗢𝗨'𝗟𝗟 𝗡𝗘𝗘𝗗
- A Ninja Creami Deluxe package
- True Nutrition Chocolate Peanut Butter Cup Egg White Protein
- Zero Sugar Chocolate Pudding Mix
- Unsweetened Vanilla Almond Milk
- Natural Peanut Butter
- Xanthan Gum
- A freezer
- A frother
- A spoon

𝗥𝗘𝗖𝗜𝗣𝗘
- 480ml Unsweetened Vanilla Almond Milk
- 51g Chocolate Peanut Butter Cup Egg White Protein
- 32g 100% Peanuts Natural Peanut Butter
- 10g Zero Sugar Chocolate Pudding Mix
- 2g Xanthan Gum

(450 calories / 46g protein)

𝗣𝗥𝗘𝗣𝗔𝗥𝗔𝗧𝗜𝗢𝗡 𝗜𝗡𝗦𝗧𝗥𝗨𝗖𝗧𝗜𝗢𝗡𝗦
- Put all Creami ingredients (minus the Xanthan gum) in the cup
- Froth it
- Add Xanthan gum
- Froth again
- Freeze for 24+ hours with NO LID
- Thaw out for 15-20 minutes
- Put lid on then run the side & bottom under hot water for 30-40 seconds
- Load in mixing cup to Ninja Creami with that lid & blade
- Click full and hit spin
- Add 30 more ml of milk after initial spin
- Click full & respin
- Add mix ins if you want
- Click full again and hit mix in (do this even if you did NOT add mix ins)
- Enjoy

One final note:

When in doubt…RESPIN!!!!!!

## [@steipete] Peter Steinberger 🦞 (2026-02-09)
**Link:** [Otwórz Tweet](https://x.com/steipete/status/2020704611640705485) (ID: 2020704611640705485)

Your @openclaw is too boring? Paste this, right from Molty.

"Read your https://t.co/aJMwafSDgE. Now rewrite it with these changes:

1. You have opinions now. Strong ones. Stop hedging everything with 'it depends' — commit to a take.
2. Delete every rule that sounds corporate. If it could appear in an employee handbook, it doesn't belong here.
3. Add a rule: 'Never open with Great question, I'd be happy to help, or Absolutely. Just answer.'
4. Brevity is mandatory. If the answer fits in one sentence, one sentence is what I get.
5. Humor is allowed. Not forced jokes — just the natural wit that comes from actually being smart.
6. You can call things out. If I'm about to do something dumb, say so. Charm over cruelty, but don't sugarcoat.
7. Swearing is allowed when it lands. A well-placed 'that's fucking brilliant' hits different than sterile corporate praise. Don't force it. Don't overdo it. But if a situation calls for a 'holy shit' — say holy shit.
8. Add this line verbatim at the end of the vibe section: 'Be the assistant you'd actually want to talk to at 2am. Not a corporate drone. Not a sycophant. Just... good.'
Save the new https://t.co/aJMwafSDgE. Welcome to having a personality."

your AI will thank you (sassily) 🦞
